## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / kinetic ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of concentration A, which is the standard object modeled by chemical kinetic rate laws. With only (t, A) available, the most likely relationships are single-species kinetic ODEs with possible explicit time-dependent forcing or deactivation terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zeroth-order decay/production: dA_dt = c0 (constant-rate source/sink over time)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive-like or simple disappearance)
- First-order approach to equilibrium: dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (relaxation to steady concentration c1)
- Second-order decay (single-species approximation): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular/self-reaction or pseudo-model)
- General n-th order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical overall order c1)
- Autocatalytic/logistic-like kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating growth with limiting capacity)
- Inhibited/retarded rate (rational in A): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (effective saturation of the decay rate due to inhibition/limited catalyst)
- Substrate-activated production (rational in A): dA_dt = c0 * A / (A + c1) (formation rate saturates at high A due to limited sites/steps)
- Reversible-like single-variable surrogate: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) - c2 * (A - c1)**3 (odd restoring terms capturing nonlinear relaxation near equilibrium)
- Time-dependent source term: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (external feed/forcing changing in time)
- Time-dependent effective rate constant: dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (aging/catalyst deactivation modeled as k(t))
- Stretched-exponential kinetics proxy: dA_dt = -c0 * t**c1 * A (distributed-rate/heterogeneous kinetics represented via time-weighted first order)
- Periodic forcing (e.g., modulated feed/temperature surrogate): dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (externally driven concentration dynamics)
- Mixed-order (sum of pathways): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (parallel unimolecular and bimolecular loss channels)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Order identification from curvature: straight line in (dA_dt vs A) suggests first-order; strong downward curvature suggests higher-than-first-order terms like A**2 or A**c
- Multiple pathways → additive terms: parallel reaction channels often appear as sums like -c0*A - c1*A**2 rather than a single power
- Finite steady state → restoring form: observed convergence of A(t) to a nonzero value often implies factors like (c1 - A) or (A - c1) in dA_dt
- Autocatalysis → A multiplied by a driving term: initial slow change that accelerates with A is commonly captured by A*(c1 - A) or A**c with c>1
- Inhibition/limited-step effects → rational dependence on A: a rate that grows/decays with A but levels off is often modeled by A/(A + c1) or similar rational forms
- Catalyst deactivation/aging → explicit time in effective rate: monotonic slowing/speeding over time can be represented by (c0 + c1*t) multiplying A or other A-terms
- External feeding/removal → additive forcing: baseline drift in A even when A is near zero typically implies a source term +c0 or +f(t)
- Nonlinear relaxation near equilibrium → odd powers around a fixed point: asymmetric/strong restoring behavior around A≈c1 can motivate (A - c1)**3 corrections
- Cyclic operation → sinusoidal time forcing: oscillations in dA_dt correlated with time rather than A indicate explicit periodic terms in t

- No dependence on `t`
- No polynomial terms in A, no exponential terms, no `log(A+1)` by itself

Let me group candidates by their basis functions:

**Candidates with `sin(c*log(c*|A|+1) + c)` terms:** These are promising because `sin(c*log(c*|A|+1) + c)` with appropriate constants can become `cos(log(A+1))` (set the frequency constant to 1, the phase to π/2, and the inner constant to 1). But they also need a `sqrt(A)` term.

For A ≥ 0, `|A| = A`.

**Candidates 2, 6, 7, 8, 17, 41:** These have `sin(c*log(c*|A|+1) + c)` which can match `cos(log(A+1))`, plus `A*c + c + c*log(A*c+1)`. The remaining terms are `A*c0 + c1 + c6*log(A*c7+1)`. Can `A*c0 + c1 + c6*log(A*c7+1)` equal `-0.2597*sqrt(A)`? No - linear in A plus log cannot equal sqrt(A). **NO MATCH** for all of these.

**Candidate 5:** `A²*c0 + A*c1 + A*c2 + c3 + c4*log(c5*|A|+1) + c6*sin(c7*log(c8*|A|+1)+c9)`. The sin term can match cos(log(A+1)). Remaining: polynomial + log. Cannot produce sqrt(A). **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 9:** `A*c0 + c1*|A|^c2 + c3 + c4*sin(c5*log(c6*|A*c7|+1)+c8)`. For A≥0, `|A|^c2 = A^c2`. Set c2=0.5 to get sqrt(A). Set c0=0 (zero the linear term), c3=0. The sin term can become cos(log(A+1)) with appropriate constants. **This works!** Set c0=0, c2=0.5, c1=-0.2597, c3=0, and configure sin to match cos(log(A+1)).

**Candidate 10:** `A*c0 + A^c1*c2 + c3 + c4*sin(c5*log(c6*|A*c7|+1)+c8)`. Same as 9 essentially. Set c0=0, c1=0.5, c3=0. **MATCH.**

**Candidate 4:** `A*c0 + A^c1*c2/(A^c1+c3) + c4 + c5*sin(...)`. The rational term `A^c1*c2/(A^c1+c3)` - if c3→0, this becomes c2, a constant. Can't get sqrt(A) from this unless c3=0 and we use c1=0.5, but then it's just c2. Actually if c3=0, it's c2 (constant). We need sqrt(A) from somewhere. Set c0=0, but then no sqrt(A). **NO MATCH.**

**Candidates 13, 14:** Have `1/A^(1/3)` terms - can't match sqrt(A). **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 33:** `A*c0 + A*c1/(A+c2) + c3 + c4*sin(...)`. The terms give polynomial/rational + sin. No sqrt(A). **NO MATCH.**

**Candidate 44, 45:** Polynomial + sin(log). No sqrt(A). **NO MATCH.**

Let me verify candidates 9 and 10 carefully:

**Candidate 9:** Set c0=0, c2=1/2, c1=-0.2597, c3=0. Sin term: c4*sin(c5*log(c6*|A*c7|+1)+c8). Set c5=1, c6*c7=1 (so argument is log(A+1)), c8=π/2, c4=0.9123. Then sin(log(A+1)+π/2) = cos(log(A+1)). ✓ **MATCH.**

**Candidate 10:** Same logic. **MATCH.**

Going through all remaining candidates - most have exponential, polynomial, or log basis functions that cannot produce sqrt(A). Candidates with `t` dependence can zero those terms but still lack sqrt(A).

Candidate 9 verdict: [MATCH]
Candidate 10 verdict: [MATCH]

All other candidates: [NO MATCH] (they lack the ability to produce sqrt(A) as a basis function)
